THE CHYRVRGIANS CLOSET: OR, An Antidotarie Chyrurgicall.

Furnished with variety and choice of: Apophlegms, Balmes, Baths, Caps,
Cataplasmes, Causticks, Carots, Clysters, Collyries, Decoctions, Diets, and
Wound-Drinks, Defensatiues, Dentifrices, Electuaries, Embrocations, Epithemes,
Errhines, Foments, Fumes, Gargarismes, Iniections, Liniments, Lotions, Oils,
Pessaries, Pills, Playsters, Potions, Powders, Qui^^^ Suppositaries, Synapismes,
Trochisces, (...), and Waters.

The greatest part whereof were scatteredly set down in sundry books and
pape^ by the Right Worshipful Mr. THOMAS BONHAM, ^r. (...) Physic; and now
drawn into method and form (...) EDWARD POETON of Petworth, (late a^^^^ng
servant to the foresaid Right Wo^^^^pfull Dr.) and published for the benefit of
his Country, and the help and ease, of young practitioners in the ancient,
necessary, and noble Science of Chyrurgerie.

LONDON, Printed by GEORGE MILLER, for EDWARD BREVVSTER, and are to be sold at
the sign of the Bible at the North door of Pa^^^. 163^.

TO THE RIGHT HONORABLE AND RIGHT virtuous Lady, FRANCIS Countess of Exceter;
EDWARD POETON of Petworth (Licentiate in Physic and Chyrurgery) wishes
abundance of internal grace; a full measure of external good things, and an
eternal and incorruptible crown of glory in the world to come.
Thrice noble, virtuous, and renowned Lady;
Having after long labor brought forth, this unpolished birth; begotten of
many Fathers (ancient, and modern) men famous (for arts) in their several
generations. I remaining no less careful for its future, prosperous
progress: then I had been laborious for its present production. I therefore
held it most necessary, to provide for it, some godly guardian, and potent
Patron to defend it from the injury of malignant Momus and his snarling,
yelping brood. But finding amongst men (to me known) none so much affecting
this noble Science as I could wish. I therefore emboldned my self (though a
stranger to your Honor) to commend it unto your Christian and noble Tutelage;
and that so much the rather, because Fames trumpet sounds forth every where
your just deserved Honor, in the love unto, (and practice of) this so noble a
Science. For be it spoken without adulation; where is there any woman living,
that has spent so much time in the study of this Art, and made so gracious and
painful a progress in the practice thereof, as your thrice noble self. Do
not the souls of the sick and sore, and the limbs of the lame, every where
(where ere you reside) bless you; proclaiming to the world, that Exceters
noble Countess abounds in mercy, charity, piety, pity, compassion, bounty,
affability, humility, hospitality, and all other commendable virtues. And
that she is constantly cheerful in the diurnall and painful performances
of these fame-meriting actions. Accept therefore I beseech your Honor of this
poor Orphan, and place it within the pale of your Potent Patronage, and let it
serve you in chief. And as you shall find its abilities and worth; so esteem
it, so commend it. And pardon I pray you, the boldness of your poor neighbor
in this attempt; And he shall ever rest during life,

Your Honors most respectively devoted in his best abilities and services,
EDWARD POETON.

TO THE RIGHT WORSHIPFVLL the Master, Wardens, Assistants, and Brotherhood of
that ancient, useful, and noble Society, the medicine Chyrurgians; the
principal members of that Society, or Corporation of the Barber Chyrurgians
of London, EDWARD POETON of Petworth wishes all happiness in this life, and
eternal felicity in the life to come.
Right worshipful,
IT is not unknown unto the most of you, that I was a long, (and the last)
servant, unto the Right Worshipful, Mr. THOMAS BONHAM Dr. of Physic; (and one
of the Assistants of your noble Society,) who whilst he lived was to me a
Master, yea more, a Father, and at his death a bountiful Benefactor; for he
gave and delivered unto me before he dyed, all his Manuscripts, both of
Physic and Chyrurgerie: the which being known unto sundry of your Society,
they requested the sight, survey, and copies of them, or of such of them as
they should best like; whereunto I yielded. But being drawn forth of the City,
unto the place where I now reside; the opportunity of satisfying their
request, and performing my promise was cut off. But not forgetting what I had
promised, as leisure would permit: I gradually composed this present Work, and
have procured it to be pressed for your service. If there be any thing in it that
may accommodate but the Junior sort of your Society; I shall be glad. If not;
I pray you accept my love therein, and I shall for ever rest,

Your Worships in his best Devotions, EDWARD POETON.

To the reading Artist.
CHristian Reader, as by former passages you may perceive the graduall
generation of this Work, so as it being now come to your hands; know that it
is more for use, then delight, unless you delight in what is useful: what is
amiss in it, I pray you pardon; what may serve your turn, use. The following
Table will direct you both to the malladie, and the medicine. The Lord bless,
guide, and prosper you: I only entreat acceptance of my good will, with your
prayers for me. From my Chamber in Petworth, in the County of Sussex.

Yours in the Lord, E. P.

Courteous reading Artist, the most remarkable errors in this present work may
(by your helping hand) be amended by the following directions. The first number
will direct you to the page: The second number stands for the line, or lines,
in which the faults are; the word or words following the letter (r.) shows how
they ought to be read. But there are some general errors, not set down by
page and line, which I entreat you to amend as you meet with them. viz. for
Mesne and Mesnes. read Mesue and M^sues for Comis read Co^u. for landani or
labdani, read ladani or laudani, for lenistici, read leuistici.

THE CHYRVRGIANS CLOSET: Or an Antidotarie Chyrurgicall. Furnished with
variety, and choice of Medicines.
Apophlegms.
. MAsticis, j. Piperis pyrethri, ana j ss. mellis q. s. s. a. f. Trochisci.
secundum magnitudinem Lupinor. One whereof being held in the mouth by the space
of half an hour fasting. *. Asswageth Andernacus.

. Masticis contritae, ss. mellis, q. s. make Trochisces in form aforesaid; One
whereof being held in the mouth as above said, and then chewed and spit forth.
*. Asswageth Andernacus.

. Masticis, j. Cort. Capparar. ij. Pyrethri, iij. Piperis, j ss. vuar.
passular, ss. Commixe them well together, and reserve them in a mass: a
portion whereof being tied up in a littell moddell, in a linen cloth, and
chewed 'twixt the teeth by the space of half an hour, (the patient being
fasting, or the stomach empty) Andernacus.

. Pyrethri, masticis, ana ssj. cerae, q.s. Make Trochisces, each singular,
about the bigness of a filberd: One whereof being chewed by the space of half
an hour together, often spitting out the Andernacus.

. Masticis, j. sem synapij, ss. piperis longi. and pyrethri, ana ij. staphidis
agriae, and piperis guiniae, ana j. mellis puri, q.s. s.a. form trochisces,
each singular, about the bigness of a small bean, to be held between the teeth
each morning fasting, by the space Poeton.

Balmes.
. Partem humani corporis incisam. Put it into a large bellied vessel of glass
(that which the Chemists call Ampulla) digest it therein for a months space,
Then make separation thereof s. a. Take of the lycour thereof lbj. theriacae
opt, vj. commixe and macerate them s.a. for xxx. days space, Then draw forth
the balm s.a. which is called a mumiated treacle. *.j. whereof commixt with
like quantity of oil of sweet almonds, and given to one who has drunk
poison, or is infected with the Pest. it speedily cures; if you cause the
patient to sweat effectually in his bed. It heales Carbuncles and the
inflammations of the sides. j. thereof taken fasting, withstands the force of
poison. Andernacus ex Paracelso.

s.a. then commixe with the distilled lycour moschi puri gra: xv. and then
reserve it for the cure both of *. wounds and ulcers. Andernacus.

basin of fair water; It will remain entire with any separation: And about the
space of one hour after it will ascend unto the top of the water, and will
there swim whole. This Balsam (being set on fire) will burn. One drop thereof
dropped hot into a pint of new milk, will coagulate the same, even like unto the
natural Balm. The first and clear water is called water of Noli *. It
strangely and speedily eases the cold gowt, a linen cloth being moystned
therewith, and applied hot Note

. Resinae terebinthinae, lbj. Thuris, Masticis, Myrrhae, Ladani, nuc: mosch.
Caryophyllor. Galangae, Zedoariae, Carpesij. ana ss. Folior: daphnoides, Pj.

. Resinae terebinthinae, lbij. olei laurini, iij. Cinamo: Spicae nardi, ana ij.
Caryophyllor, no: 50. folij, ij, Euphorbij, Baccar: Lauri, gum: Hederae, ana
ss. Galbani, Castorei, Cyperi, ana vj. Tegular. bis Coctar. and in oleo Communi
extinctar. lbss. Beat the tiles into fine powder and cast that powder into the
bottom of a Curcubit. The other ingredients being duly prepared, place them
on the top of that powder within the Curcubit, then lute on the head (with a
beak) and set to the receiver. Then begin the distillation with a gentle fire
until the water be drawn forth, and the oil begin to appear, then change
the receiver, and increase the fire a little, until that the oil be
exhausted, and the Balm begin to show it self: Then change the receiver
again, and augment the fire, unto a strong heat, and so continue it until
that the Balm be all come forth. Then reserve with carefullnesse, each apart
by it self. The water is of like virtue with other waters of the most
excellent artificial Balmes. The oil is no whit inferior unto any other oil
of Balsam. The viz. The Palsy of the Mouth, Tongue, and Yard. The Epilepsie,
Trembling or shaking of the members. Dolours of the Back, Raines, Sinews, and
Joints, being inwardly administered and outwardly applied. It Is of rare force
against the bitings, or stingings of Scorpions, Serpents, Mad dogs, and other
venomous creatures. By the same reason, if any one be poisoned with Henbane,
Hemlocks, Opium, or any the like cold poison. This being drunk with pure wine
hot, and the body be therewith outwardly anointed, it expels the poison and
restores health. It restores speech lost: It cures Strumes: It takes away proud
and corrupt flesh in ulcers. It strengthens the memory, if the hinder part of
the head be therewith anointed. Being dropped into the Ears, it cures Deafness:
It cease the Toothache: It puts away the Colic, arising from cold, windy,
or gross vapors. Note that neither the water, nor yet the Balm, is inwardly
to be administered, unless it be mixed with some appropriate lycour. Reubeus.

. Terebinthinae purae, lbij. latirum antiquor. in oleo iasmino extinctor. q. s.
macis, and styracis, ana j. belzoini. ss. Prepare, commixe, and distill them

, Terebinthinae purae vj. aloes been tritae, j. Masticis, Galangae,
Caryophyllor, nuc: myrist: Cinamo: Zedoariae, Cubebar. ana j. gum: ficuum, vj.
The needful things being well beaten, incorporate the whole, and so enclose it
in a limbeck, that nothing may expire: then place the limbeck in a furnace, and
according to art, with a gentle fire, draw forth the lycours. Note this, that
the milder the fire shall be, the sweeter shall be the water, which will be
likewise clear as fountain water. The second lycour will be thick, and of a
saffron color, and will swim ^n the top of the first. The third lycour will
come forth like unto clear honey; the which when you shall perceive, then
change the receiver, and augment your fire a littell, and you shall receive a
Balm of rare and excellent virtues. This tried by water remains entire as
does the natural Balm. The several names of these lycours are so well known
to every Artist that I omit to set them down: their virtues follow. The water
cures *. ouer-moist Eyes, Soreness, and swellings of the Eyelids, if Noli me
tangere, Gowtes proceeding from a cold cause; Eroding ulcers, Bruises, Palsies.
In sum all greefes of the sinews, arising from cold and moisture. Mr. Sherly.

. Terebinthinae optimae, lbj. olei laurini, iiij. gum: el^mi, iij. ss galbani,
iij. thuris, myrrhae, gum: hederae, Caryophyllor, Symphiti, minoris, Cinamoni,
nucis moschatae, zedoariae, zinzib, dictamni albi, ana j. olei lumbricor, ij.
aq: vitae, lbvj. Powder what is requisite, and infuse them altogether in the aq:

. Olei omphacini, lbij, Styracis Calamitae, Ladani, Thuris Masculi, Croci, gum:
arabici, rubeae tinctor, gum: hederae aloes Succor, Masticis, Cariophyllor.
Cinamomi, Galangae, nucis moschatae, Cubebar, ana ij. gum: elemi, lbj, myrrhae,
bdellij, ana j. Sagapeni, ammoniaci, opoponacis, ana x. Stamp what is to be

Curcubit, and lute on the head, then set it to a gentle fire, (for the first
xij. hours) and set to the receiver. Then for vj. hours more, increase the
fire s.a. unto the perfection of the distillation: The whole humor being drawn
forth, stamp the faeces, and incorporate them with the former extracted
lycour, and redistill them as before. Repeat the same method a third time, so
shall you attain a substance having all the notes, and virtues Lues venerea.
It cures the Epilepsie; if for thirty days space (each several day) the
Coronall future be therewith artificially anointed: And likewise that one
spoonefull thereof commixt with like proportion of the powder of the roots of
Paeonie, be inwardly taken each day fasting. It cures a Quartane Agew, at the
fourth fit, if ss. thereof mixed with generous wine, be administered before the
invasion of the fit. It maruelously cheeres the heart by putting away
melancholy and sadness: It preserves the lungs: It Is good against all cold
affects, whether inward, or outward. A purple cloth madefied therein, and
applied to the Temples; cures the Megrim, and the Vertigo. It opens
obstructions, Strengthens the brain, Cures deafness, Cease conuulsions and
the resolution of the sinews, And heals any green wound. Vigo.

short space) shall be perfectly healed. Rulandus.

. Calcis non extinctae ix. ciner. de cerro^ (which Dyers use) on these power as

till the ashes and Calx have yielded their force. Then clear out the water,

. Lixiuijfortiss. lbij. vitrioli albi iiij. Calcis vinae opt: combustae, Mix

. Calcis viuae opt, lbj. Burn the same again in a fire of Charcoales by the
space of iij. or iiij. hours; after powder it finely, and put it in lixiuij
barbitonsoris lbij. boil them together in a brass pan till it be thick,
hereof you may make tents and trochises, round, flat, and every form that may
serve your purpose. Reserve them in a glass vessel close stopped. When occasion
inuites their use, wet one side of them with your spettle, and lay it to the
Balthrop.

. Ciner. tartari glauci, sextarium vnum, Ciner. quercinor. been mundator. and
Calcis viuae been vstae, ana lbj. Steep all these in ij. gallons of water, and
stir it iij. or iiij. times in xxiiij. hours, then set it over a fire of
coals, and let it boil a little, after that let it stand to settle xij.
hours, then strain the cleerest of the lycour through a double woollen cloth,
so that no ashes may go through, but only the clear lycour. Set that over
the fire, and continue the ebulition, until it attain the thickness and
hardness of salt; then separate it with a knife into small pieces, and reserve
them in a double glass close from the air (else it will s.a. opens and
breaks hard Tumors, nodes, or knots (which cannot be resolved) which are
fixed to the bones of the arms, or legs. Clowes.

. Calcis viuae, vitrioli, salis petri, and aluminis rochae, ana q s. Beat them
all into powder, and put that powder into an earthen pot which is made full of
holes in the bottom, then take strong soape lees q.s. power the same into the
pot (where the powder is) and let it draine forth into some fit vessel, then
stir up the powder, and power on the Lees again, and let it draine as
before, let it be often repeated: Lastly, boil the lycour as the former was
boiled, unto the hardness of salt, and so reserve it, *. for Clowes.
Calmetheus calls it, lapis infernalis.

. Lixiuij acerrimi Saponarij, lbij vitrioli rom: salis ammoniaci, and ^itri,
ana j. Let these be well beaten, and after dissolved with the Lee, then add
thereto opij thebaici, ss. Boil them altogegether, with a gentle fire, until
it attain the form of a stone, then reserve it. *. This works without any

. Mercurij sublimat, ij. ss. vng. popul. iij. opij gr. v lap. haematit, ss.

Cerots.
. Ladani puri and been olentis, j ss. lig: aloes, ss. masticis, and thuris, ana

. Lytharg. lap: haematit, sang: drac, bol: arm: opij, masticis, ammoniaci,

iij. ros. rub: myrrhae, aloes, ana gra. xviij. Succi hypocislidis, gallar.
immaturar. balaustior. aristoloch: rot: ana vj. visci quercini, and terebinth,
ana ij. Sang: homis: rufi, ix. Form it as follows. Take a whole rams skin
(new flaide) wool and all; Cut it into pieces, and boil it in water, until
the substance of the skin be dissolved, then strain it, and take of the
strained lycour, lbj. Put it into a new vessel, and at a gentle fire dissolve
therein the misle of the oak (stirring it constantly) then put in the worms,
then add the wax, turpentine, and the mastick. These being molten, add the
gummes (being first dissolved in vinegar) lastly, cast in the other
ingredients, (having first powdered, and scarsed such as need) boil and stir
it to the form of a Cerot. Then work it with your hands, and reserve it in a
Arnoldus Villanouanus.

moystned with oil of bares) work in the saffron being made into fine powder)
and so with diligence s. a. make a mass thereof and reserve it. Nicolaus.

. Saniculae, Sanamundae, rumicis, canabis, Sem: caulium rubr: consolidae

aequales, make it as aforesaid. Vel.. Apij, arnoglossae, Lanceolatae,
Sanamundae, Consolidae vtriusque, Rubiae, and canlae. Vel.. Sanamundae,
Pimpinellae, Saluiae, Cardui benedicti, Agrimoniae, pedis Columbini, Plantag.
Centinodij, Linguae auis, and Spergulae, prepare these as the first. Vel..
Sanamundae, Betonicae, Saluiae, Hederae terrest: Agrimoniae, Pilosellae,
Pimpinellae, Violariae, Plantag. Molaginis. Draw out the juice of these
herbs, and boil it with wine, then give it to drink; but observe, that you
daily withdraw of the quantity of your Melag. which was added, to prevent an
over speedy closing of the wound at the first. Vel.. Angellicae, Betonicae,
Agrimoniae, Pilosellae, Hoderae terrestis, Septem meruiae violariae, but the
least of the Angelica. Boil them in wine, let the Patient drink of it thrice
a day, the oftener the sooner whole. Vel.. Betonicae, Agrimoniae, Fragariae,
Asari, Violariae, Linguae bouis, Ambrosij, Plantaginis, Quinque folij,
Hyperici, Spicae, Linguae auis, Pimpinellae, ana Mj. Stamp and boil them in
wine, strain them, and add thereto, Mellis q.s. and if the party have no
fever, then add one hundred grains of pepper. Another much commended by the
Author; Is to be made ex Caul rubr: and rubia, and teneritatibus rumicis, and
Sem: Canabis, vel teneritate ipsius herbae and Sanamunda, and consolida minore,
and Sanicula, of each a like proportion, save that you must double the portion
of the rubia; Stamp, and boil the herbs in wine, to the wasting of the
third part; you may (for Gilbert. Rules observed by the Author in the ordaining
of the drinks. First, that if there be any danger of a fever, that then he
made these drinks with water and sugar, and not with wine and honey. Secondly,
that the Patients diet, should be free from milk, cheese, eggs, fruits, and
flesh of vngelded beasts or fowls, and that he eat unleavened bread. As for
carnal copulation, all other authors forbid. Further observations of the same
author. Give unto a wounded person to drink Succi pilosellae, if he cast it
again (in what part soever the wound be) he shall die; but if he retain it,
he shall live. Then for the first, give him to drink, plantaginem and
fragariam. The second day, give him the same again garyophillatam being
thereto added. The third day, add pilosellam to the former. The fourth day do
as ye did on the third. The fifth day, add to the former, hederam terrestrem;
the which continue until the seventh day. After which, you shall decline your
method, as you did formerly augment it, until you come to the herbs of the
first day, wherewith you began. Another order practiced by some, and recorded
by our Author. First, they wash the wound with warm water: Next they apply the
lard of bacon, stamped with wormwood, for iij. days: After that, whites of
eggs with flax, for four days. In the mean time, they give also a drink
made ex vino vel: ceruisia and mediate mellis, with which is also boiled Succus
Consolide mino, and Saniculae, and Absinthij, and Faeniculi; of which they gave
every morning a full cup fasting, which would issue out of the wound, and
mitigate pain; The wound being thus mundified, they applied to consolidate it
that which follows. Olibani, Sarcocolla ana pares portiones, aloes quantum
est medium istor. Make them in fine powder, which then shall consolidate the
wound in ij. days, though it be very large. Also puluis cornu ceruini,
shuts up a wound, and takes away the moist disposition. Gilbert.

and reserve the lycour in a clean close vessel for use. Let the Patient drink
hereof in the morning xviij. blood-warme, and about two hours after let him
drink lbj. more, blood-warme as before, and one hour after that lbj more, and
about four or five of the clock in the afternoon, xv. more, remembering
always to drink it warm. Let the Patient so order the business, that he may
have four or five stools within the compass of a natural day, but not to
exceed five stools, and let him drink more in the forenoone then in the
afternoon, that he be not forced to rise in the night, least he take cold. Let
the Patient use a very slender diet the first eight days, eating very little.
After that he may somewhat enlarge his Diet, for seven days following, with
this caution, that he still leave off with some appetite. Let him continue the
Drink as he finds the working thereof: for it is both Diet and purging. *
It Is excellent for all aches, benumbed members and all old painful diseases
Note. If the Patient be of a weak stomach, then mix a spoonful or two of
syrup of Roses, and a few drops of Cinnamon water with the first draught that he
drinks in the morning. And let him observe this Diet following: viz. To eat
but of one sort of meat at one meal, and let that meat be either Veale,
Mutton, Capon, Chicken, or Rabbet, using his Drink as before. Let his bread be
made as follows: viz.. Scobs Guiaci, iiij. steep it in lbxij. of pure water
warm in a close earthen pot the space of twelve hours, then boil it to the
wasting of a third part of the water, afterward strain it until it be
clear, then add to th lycour fine sugar in powder, lb ss. of the powders of
Annisseeds and Coriander-seeds prepared, I had this receipt of Master Henry
Fish, brother unto Master Fish, the Chamberlain of London.
ana ij. With fine Wheate-flower, q.s. make paste, whereof make cakes, and bake
them thoroughly, till they be hard and dry, which are to be eaten in stead of
bread with his meat. Before he enter into the Diet, let him do as follows..

. Cinabrij, ss. thuris, masticis, ana j. Calami aromat, Zedoariae, ana iij.
o^ibani, Sandaracae verae, ana ij Cerussae, ss. Terebinth: q.s.f Trochis. Vel.
Cort. thurit, ij. masticis, gummi hederae, gummi iuniperi, ladani,
hypocistidis, ana ss. auripigmenti rubri, vel citrini, iij. Cinabri, j.
Terebinth, q.s.f. Trochis. Vel. Cinabrij, ij. ladani, ij. Cort: citri Sicci,
ss. Sublimati, j. thuris, masticis, styracis, calamitae, rad: dictamni very,
ana jss. theriacae veteris, q.s. Form trochises, each several to weigh jss.
The Author (as he affirms) never used Fume if by any other means he could
prevail, by reason of ill accidents, which he had observed in other men's
practice. viz. That sundry of the noble parts had received hurt thereby. In
some has chanced the Syncop: In some the Palsy: In other some Conuulsions,
etc. But if necessity compelled; he ever used one of these three here set
down. Further, observing these rules. viz. That if any flux descend to the
lungs, in stead of the Sublimate he used auripigmentum. Secondly, when he used
the Fume after the unction, to extirpate the relics of the grief, that then
he omitted both the Cynabrium: as also the auripigmentum, and in their steades
he commixt with the other ingredients some proper Cordials, forcible to cut,
attenuate, and to discuss. Thirdly, he administered his Fumes in this form:
viz. he placed his patient naked under a canopie on a fit seat, causing him to
shut his eyes; Sometimes he gave liberty to put forth his head. He spent at
once j. or jss. of the Trochises. He further used the bed (after the Fume) and
enlarged the sweat, Secundum vires. Fourthly, he administered the fume in the
morning fasting; unless that the Patient were very weak; then he gave
liberty for the yolke of an egg and a little wine, or else diamargaritonis
frigid. ss. or a little of the bark of a Citron condited. *. In the cure of
Lues Venerea. Antonius

. Vitrioli albi, iiij. aluminis vsti, ij. Make them into fine powder, put them

excellent virtue, against Fistulaes and hollow Ulcers being iniected hot, and
presently to shut or closed up the orifice, that none of the lycour may issue

will produce an Escar: Then unclothe it, and iniect aq: plantaginis warm,
reclose the orifice, like space of time as before. In which proportion of time,
the pain will cease, and the heat will be allayed, then vncloathe it again,
and iniect of these oils being mixed. viz. Ol: lilior. albor. hypericonis,
rosar. lumbricor. ana j. Ol: Spicae ss. misce. This being iniected, close, and
cloth it up, suffering it so to rest by the space of a day natural. Then
reiniect more of those the oils, closing, clothing, and suffering it to rest
xxiiij. hours as before. Repeat this iniection of the oils, and the other
operations unto the fourth time. Then shall you see abundance of sanious and
putrid humors to slow forth, the which you shall wash off with water (warm) by
iniection. Let this course be iudiciously prosecuted unto perfection of cure.
But Note; that if the ulcer wax exceeding tender, that then it is behoofefull,
to weaken the strength of the water, which you may discern by the touch of
your tongue. The Author professes that, with these iniections he has cured
many Fistulaes, Hollow Ulcers, Caruncles, and such like. And that with the
water he has cured Scabs, Wheales, Itch, etc. He also affirms it to be
profitable against burnings or skaldings, first to be washed with this: and
after with plantane water. Ex Manuscripto.

Lotions.
. Chamo. Saluiae, origani, betonicae, ana M j. Boil them in Lee made with
rain water and good ashes, strain and reserve it. The day before the use
hereof.. Ros. rub. maioranae, lauendalae, rorismar. Spicae, betonicae, ana P j.
agarici concisi, ij. Shred the herbs and mix them with the Agarick, put them
into a fit bag, madefie the same in the former decoction, suffer it there to
remain by the space of a night. In the morning (the Patient being fasting)
wash well the head, with that lycour, and with a sweet ball; then rub the head
well, with the bag wrung hot out of the lycour. Lastly, dry it with clean,
dry, and hot Andernacus.

Oils.
The true manner or method of preparing Oils, as it is prescribed by that
learned Quercitanus.

. Olei omphacini, q.v. wash well the oil in the distilled water, of common
water, after that purify the oil in B. M. until there remain no faeces..
Huius olei sic praeparati lbj. ros. rub. ex vnguibus expurgatar. (well stamped
in a mortar) lbj ss. put them together into a glass matrat, well closed; place
it in hot prepared horse-dung to putrify, by the space of xij. days. Then
make a strong expression, and cast away the faeces: Add like quantity of Roses
(prepared as the former) again unto the oil, using the former method for
putrefaction, and expression; repeat it a third time: So shall you attain a
far better Oil, then that which is commonly sold by the Apothecaries. But if
you will make oils more forcible to heat, attenuate and digest. Then take of
your purified oil as before, and of spirit of wine, of each like portion, so
may you make oil, ex baccis lauri, etc. But these ought to digest a months
space in horse-dung, and so to express and repeat as before. But the best and
strongest of all (which we call Chimicall) are drawn without addition of oil,
unto any the materials, only with spirit of wine, and that in Balneo vaporoso.
Thus having set down this so general a method; I purpose therefore (...),
only to express the virtues of such oils as are made of one simple. But in
compounds to follow mine Authors.

Oleum ammoniaci chym: extract. *. Expels sand and Andernacus.

Oleum terebinthinae chym: extract: *. Commodious against all Asthma, or
difficulty of breathing, if ij. thereof be taken every morning with some
convenient broth or lycour, until the desire of the Patient be accomplished.
It auailes against Empyema, or any other ill affects of the Thorax, springing
virid: aeris ana parts aequas, and duly apply it. Andernacus.

Oleum Salis. Commixt with the oils, of Wax, Turpentine, s.a. *. This
maruelously mitigateth the pains of the Gout. It breaks the stone, and sends
it forth, being outwardly applied to the region of the Raynes. One drop thereof
being mixed with some appropriate lycour, and daily taken by the mouth, puts
away the deformed color of the skin. Three drops thereof mixed with like
quantity of pure aq: vitae, being accustomably (taken fasting) once in vij.
days; preserves youth, in such as are young, and renewes youth in such as are
aged. It consumes the water which is between the flesh and the skin, by
outward application. It cures the Epilepsie: Heales the Iandise: Drives away
Agues: Dissolues Conuulsions; and cures Abcessions. Andernacus.

Oleum tartari, being mixed with mumia, and applied. *. Cures eroding ulcers.
Being drunk with wine, it breaks the stone in the raynes, expels the gravel,
and prouokes urine. Andernacus.

. Olei comis veteris lbiij. terebinth: abietinae, lbij. vini albi veteris and

Aparitius de Zubia: Chirurgus Italus.

Oleum Sampsuchinum. *. Refreshes wearied Limbs; profits much against cold
affects of the brain and Synewes. It much accommodates such as are Paraletick,
if the spine of the back be therewith well anointed in the Bath. It puts away
the torturing Cramp of the Laws, by being iniected into the nostrills. It
disperseth flatuosities within the Cranium, by sending it into the Ears. It
auailes against the bitings of Scorpions. Cordus.

Oleum amygd. dulc. *. Makes smooth the roughness of the Asperiteria, and
opens the suffocated longs. It moystens and softens the hardness and dryness
of the joints. It Is not only pleasant in meats, but much profits such as
are either Hectic, or Phthisick. It fattens lean bodies. It increases
Sperme. It mitigates the violence of the Cough. Being iniected, It allayeth the
acrimonie and sharpness of urine, and heals the excoriated writers. Cordus.

Oleum raphaninuns. *. Auailes much against Phtyhriaseos, or the lousy evil.
It frees the skin from Scurf, and Scabs. Dioscorides.

Ol: macis chym: extract: is virtuously hot. *. It assuageth the Euonymus.

Oleum Sulphuris chym: extract: *. Auailes in greefes, arising viz. in Fevers,
putrid, tertians, quotidians, quartanes. The Pest. In wounds, and ulcers,
hollow and sinowie. In many affects of the brain, mouth, teeth, stomach,
liver, spleen, matrixe, bladder, intestines, and ioynt^. In chief, such as
spring either from putrefaction, or plenitude of humors. The dose is so much as
will be taken up with a feather of a pullen; dipped into, and drawn forth (...)
some appropriate distilled water, wine, decoction, etc. viz. In a quotidian, in
wine, wherein has been decocted Mints, or Rosemarie; to be taken a little
before the invasion of the fit. In a Tertian; in wine, wherein has been
decocted, Centory. In a quartane; with buglosse water. In the Pest. in wine
decocted with radishes, and commixt with Andromachus Treacle, and Mithridate.
It heals Ulcers and Pustules of the mouth, being applied softly with a
feather. It profits in the Epilepsie, administered with the decoction of Betony,
and Paeonie. In the Cough: in wine, wherein has been decocted, nettle seeds,
and hyssope. In queasinesse of the stomach, with worme-wood water. In dolor of
the stomach, and Collicke arising from wind; in water of Camomill. In
coldness of the liver, and dropsy: with waters of Ireos, Celandine, and
honey. In obstruction of the spleen: with water of tamarisk. In Lues Venerea:
in water of fumitary, or in water of broom flowers. Against worms: in water
of grass or of wormwood. In greefes of the Matrixe: in wine, decocted with
Betony, and Mother-wort. In suppression of urine: in wine, decocted with
garlic. In the cold gout: in water of Chamaepiteos. In the toothach: to be
applied only with a feather, unto the tooth or teeth affected, but if all the
teeth be affected, then to commixe a drop or two with the decoction of Mints,
and to hold it in the mouth. In all wounds, or ulcers, lightly to be applied
with a feather. Euonymus.

Oleum ligni guiaci, chym: extract. *. Is of excellent virtue against dolors,
and ulcers, concomitating Lucs Venerea. Euonymus.

Oleum Caryophyllor. chym: extract: *. Is hot and dry in the third degree. It
comforts, and strengthens the stomach, the liver, and the heart. It stays the
flux Diarrhaea. Auailes against cold and moisture. It attenuates, and
dissipates, gross, melancholy spirits. It has all the virtues of Balsam. It
strengthens the brain, and the visiue spirits. Auailes against Vertigo: if
iij. or iiij. drops thereof, be taken in the morning fasting, in some
appropriate matter. It stays rhewmes. Euonymus.

Oleum spicae, chym: extract: *. Heales the Gonorrhaea, if the raines be
therewith anointed. It expels worms, if ij. drops thereof be ^iuen in wine. In
sum it is endued with many excellent virtues, as being profitable against all
cold and moist affects. Euonymus.

Oleum e baccis iuniperichym: extact: *. Is full fraught with virtues. It
eases the torment of the intestines; if iij. or iiij. drops thereof be
administered in good wine. It stays Gonorrhaea; by anointing of the raines
therewith. It Is comparable (in many things) with Balsam. It preuents swounding;
in those who are thereunto subject; and recouers them being in it, if iij. or
iiij. drops thereof be given with spirit of wine. It Is good against resolution
of the sinews, and all cold affects of the brain. It preserues the body
against venomous and pestilent air. It restores a decayed stomach. It stays
vomiting, and fluxes of the nether belly. It kills worms. Stays spitting of
blood. Heales the landise. Helps conuulsed members; being outwardly applied.
It cures inueterate and malign scabs. Heales the grief of the fundament,
called Condyloma. Heales Chaps of the hands. Eases the gout of the feet, and
huckle bone. And being applied to the Navel: it helps the Colic. Euonymus.

Oleum antimonij, seu sanguis stibij, is thus made. Reguli antimonij q.v.
grind it most finely upon a marble stone, pouring still unto it a little
distilled vinegar: when it is perfectly ground, put it into a clean felt, and
pour of your vinegar gradually upon it, until it have dissolved and carried
through all the Antimonie into the vessel that stands under to receive it:
then put all that lycour into a limbeck, and distill it out; the faeces
remaining in the bottom will be red, which take and put in a cloth, hang the
same in some moist place, with a receiver under it to drop into, and that which
so resolves and droppeth down, reserve as excellent, against * creeping, and
malign ulcers: Your Regulus is thus made.. Stibij q.v. Melt, and let it cool
again, remelt, and let it cool again; repeat it five or six times, until
it be perfect. Fallopius. Gesner. Affirms that this oil assuageth the
dolors of wounds; and perfectly cures any wound whatsoever. He likewise extols
it as wonderful in curing Cancrous, and Contumacious Ulcers.

Oleum Castorinum. *. Mightily auailes against all cold affects; in chief, in
neruous parts. It heales the Palsy, Cramps, Conuulsions, etc. It preuents the
sharp, and shaking vigor and rigor of Agues: if the spine of the back be
therewith anointed, before the invasion of the fit. Iacobus de Manlijs.

Oleum de Capparibus. *. Good against hardness, and stopping of the Spleen,
and other consimilar greefes thence arising. Innominatus.

Oleum nicotianae. *. Good in wounds; against scabs, and ulcers. It assuageth
headache. Innominatus.

Oleum rosatum. *. Allayeth inflammations, assuageth dolor, abateth tumor, and
gently resolves; Corroborateth those parts which are neruous. Innominatus.

Oleum menthae. *. Heates, and strengthens a cold weak stomach, stays
vomiting, stirs up appetite, and helps concoction. Innominatus.

Oleum absinthij. *. Heates and strengthens parts weakened through cold, in
chief, the stomach; it stirs up appetite, opens obstructions, kills worms.
Innominatus.

Oleum lileaceum. *. Heats, resolves, and digests. It Is profitable against cold
affects of the neck, thorax, stomach, matrix, and bladder. Innominatus.

Oleum anethinum. *. Assuageth pains, opens the pores, resolves Apostemes and
hard Tumors, abates the rigor of Fevers, prouokes both sweat and sleep.
Innominatus.

Oleum rutaceum. *. Opens, heateth, resolves and mitigateth dolor. It
warmeth the raynes, matrix, and bladder, assuaging their pains. It helps the
Colic, if the belly be therewith anointed hot, or a simple Clister thereof
administered. It comforts the nerves, abates the vigor of the Cramp, and expels
cold humors. Innominatus.

little Opium with your Anodinall ingredients, and therewith to cloth or arm

sharpness of such grief or pain. But this rule must, be observed, that no
opiated Pessary may be permited to remain (within the Matrix) above the space
of one half hour, least that thereby the membranous and neruous parts, should
any way be hurt. Andernacus.

Turpentine. These being incorporated, suffer them a little to cool, then
gradually put in the remaining ingredients, being well beaten and finely
searsed, stir it constantly, until you be able to endure your hands
therein, then kneade it effectually with your hands, until all the moisture be
euaporated, then remoysten it with goats milk, and work it still with your
hands unto the perfect body of a Plaster, then from those who have fallen from
on high. It restores lost flesh. In sum, it mundifieth, digesteth, and
cicatrizeth. Andernacus.

. Cerae nouae citr. thuris, Santali, ana ij. terebinth: aceti fortiss. j. Mix

plaster in form of a Cap, or otherwise as in your judgment you shall see
cause; now is the skull be fractured, against that place the plaster will be
much dryer then elsewhere, and this will be manifest in three days space, but
if the plaster be equal an uniform, then judge the skull to be whole.
Arceus.

. Galbani, and opoponacis, ana ij. ammoniaci, bdellij, ana iij. Beat them as
small as you can, and put them into a new, and well leaded earthen pot, which
will contain iij. pintes, and power upon them, aceti fortiss: lbj. then cover

unto them, aceti fort: iiij. and stir them well together, then set them over
a gentle fire, that the gummes may dissolve by degrees. Note; that you forget
not at any time to cease stirring; your gummes being dissolved, strain them
through a piece of new, thin, and strong canuasse; let your pot be clean
wiped, and then put your gummes into it again, and gently, and carefully (at a
soft fire) euaporate the vinegar, so stirring the gummes that they burn not,
and be watchful that nothing fall into them. Then take Cerae nonae (thin
shaven) lb ss ol: oliuar. lbij. Melt these together in a fit vessel, on a
gentle fire, then put into them, lythargyri auri been tri^i, lbj ss. stir

then take heed that your fire be very small, and put in your gummes by degrees,
about the quantity of a nut at once, it will require an hours space to put
them in, be careful to stir them with diligence, and watch that they boil
not over: Then add thereto, aristolochiae vtriuqsque, calaminaris, myrrhae,
thuris, (subtle: pull.) ana j. terebinth: purae iiij. ol: laurini j. Insperse
the pouders gradually, that they knot not together, and take it off the fire

must be done by degrees; then set it our a heat of embers, and stir it till
it attain a due consistence, then pour it into cold water, and work it up

together, reserve it (in rowles) in oyled paper, or oyled leathe, or both, and
new oil the paper once a year, and so keeping it from sun and wind, it
will remain in force, for fifty years space, and be then as good as at the
first making. Vel.. Ol: comis: lbij. Cerae nona, lbj. lytharg: auri, lbj ss.

and rad: ireos, ana j. lap: calaminaris, myrrhae, ana j. ol: laurini, and gummi
elemi, ana j. terebinth: venetae, iiij. Dissolve the galbanum, opoponax: the
amoniacum and the bdellium, in strong vinegar; dissolve the gum: elemum, in the
oil of bays; powder, and searse what is requisite, and proceed according to
the form of the precedent plaster, unto the finishing and reserving hereof.
These playsters accord Anthonies fire, and shingles. They assuage pain, and
therefore profit in aches. They are useful in wounds of all sorts. Cap a pe.
They confirm dislocations. They cure foynes and thrusts, without tenting, if
they matter not before the first application. Note; that this plaster,
destroys not any dead, or proud flesh; so that such ought to be removed before
it be applied. Paracelsus.

would have him wake, mix vinegar with salt, and rub his temples therewith, and
he will awake right soon. Ex Manuscripto antiquissimo.

: Occulor. cancror. f. Pull. Subtilissimus. *. To conioyne, or s.a. and roll it
up with a fit linen rowler, hot and dry, so as no moisture may come into or
near the wound; let it thus remain by the space of xxiiij. hours. History.
It chanced to one thus dressed, that before the time came to open it, that the
rowler slipped besides the wound: The Surgeon being recalled, beheld this
disaster with much grief; and with all care, haste, and diligence, he
reappareld it, and coming the second day after, upon vncloathing thereof, he
found a perfect union. Ranzouius.

Synapismes.
. Ficuum ping. Macerate them in hot water xxiiij. hours, then express them
strongly, and stamp them exactly; stamp likewise Sem: synapi q.s. adding

the former lycour incorporate, and apply it. If you require it in a mean; make
it of equal mixture: If weak, then inuert your order, viz. Take ij. parts of
the fig paste, and but one part of the other. In delicate and rare skins, add
micar panis being first madified in aceto. *. This auailes in old greefes
arising from cold, against the falling sickness, the vertigo, universal
hedache, the megrim, aches of the joints, sinews, and hips. Aetius.
